  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_d5401491-907a-44d3-91d9-c50c2bc4f4f8'
      });

              <span id="reviewTextContainer846480796" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer5992377112202595557"><b>Nothing Lasts Forever, Sidney Sheldon </b><br/><br/>This medical thriller tells the story of three female doctors trying to prove themselves in a profession dominated by men. Each of them has their own story, and each of their tales are well connected and intertwined with each other. But suddenly there is chaos, one dies, another is about to get the hospital shut down, and the third faces the death penalty for murder.<br/><br/>عنوانها: هیچ چیز جاودانه نیست؛ هیچ چیز ابدی نیست؛ نویسنده: سیدنی شلدون؛ تاریخ نخستین خوانش: ر</span>
  <span id="freeText5992377112202595557" style="display:none"><b>Nothing Lasts Forever, Sidney Sheldon </b><br /><br />This medical thriller tells the story of three female doctors trying to prove themselves in a profession dominated by men. Each of them has their own story, and each of their tales are well connected and intertwined with each other. But suddenly there is chaos, one dies, another is about to get the hospital shut down, and the third faces the death penalty for murder.<br /><br />عنوانها: هیچ چیز جاودانه نیست؛ هیچ چیز ابدی نیست؛ نویسنده: سیدنی شلدون؛ تاریخ نخستین خوانش: روز دهم ماه ژوئن سال 1996میلادی<br /><br />عنوان: هیچ چیز جاودانه نیست؛ نویسنده: سیدنی شلدون؛ مترجم: نفیسه معتکف؛ تهران، فرهنگ جامع، 1373؛ در 211ص؛ موضوع: داستانهای نویسندگان امریکایی - سده 20م<br /><br />عنوان: هیچ چیز جاودانه نیست؛ نویسنده: سیدنی شلدون؛ مترجم: فریده مهدوی دامغانی؛ تهران، درسا، 1387؛ در 596ص؛ شابک 9780646104259؛<br /> <br />سرگذشت سه زن پزشک (دکتر پیچ تیلور، دکتر کیث ترنر، و دکتر هانی تافت) را بازگو میکند، که میخواهند خود را در شغلی که مردان در آن چیره تر هستند، پایدار و پابرجا کنند؛ سه دکتر جوان با امیدها، رؤیاها، و آرزوهای دور و درازشان، که هر یک داستان خویشتن را دارد، اما سرگذشت هرکدام به خوبی با سرنوشت دیگری، پیوند خورده است؛ ناگهان غوغایی از راه میرسد؛ ...؛ <br /><br />تاریخ بهنگام رسانی 23/07/1399هجری خورشیدی؛ ا. شربیانی</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6475810038113477694">It actually shocked me that I haven't really reviewed any book from my favorite author. Yes, Sidney Sheldon is my favorite author. Heard that right. Quite surprising for a 14 year old who's fond of reading Young Adult fiction, eh?<br/><br/>This book was actually gripping. Everytime I let go of it, it makes me wanna cradle it in my arms and murmur, "I'm sorry for putting you down. Let me continue reading you."   <span id="freeText6475810038113477694" style="display:none">It actually shocked me that I haven't really reviewed any book from my favorite author. Yes, Sidney Sheldon is my favorite author. Heard that right. Quite surprising for a 14 year old who's fond of reading Young Adult fiction, eh?<br /><br />This book was actually gripping. Everytime I let go of it, it makes me wanna cradle it in my arms and murmur, "I'm sorry for putting you down. Let me continue reading you." So this story was mainly about a female doctor who had a patient who seemingly hates her. And this certain patient had asked the doctor to kill him because 'he can't take the pain anymore', and so she did. She committed euthanasia. The doctor thought that that's all to it. End of story. But afterwards, she discovered that her patient had given her an inheritance. Lots of lots of money. So other people had thought of her as purposely murdering the patient. The chapters, aside from the prologue mainly tells what happened before the event until the end of the event.<br /><br />Actually, the story wasn't really appealing for me. It wasn't all that great. It wasn't that bad either. I like this author mainly because of his writing style. Weird eh? But his writing style if honestly the best I've ever read. Fast paced, but not leaving any important details. He's just awesome.<br /><br />So all in all, I give this 4 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6475810038113477694" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_586175512" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/586175512" />
    <a title="Sully (thysaltymar)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9986049-sully-thysaltymar"><img alt="Sully (thysaltymar)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600734096p2/9986049.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/586175512?book_show_action=true">Apr 09, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sully (thysaltymar)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sully (thysaltymar)" href="/user/show/9986049-sully-thysaltymar">Sully (thysaltymar)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9986049-sully-thysaltymar?shelf=favorite">favorite</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9986049-sully-thysaltymar?shelf=owned-books">owned-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer586175512" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3821538866816513868">“You have two choices. you can keep running and hiding and blaming the world for your problems, or you can stand up for yourself and decide to be somebody important.” —Sidney Sheldon, Nothing Lasts Forever<br/><br/>Once again, I owe my life to Sidney Sheldon (<i>over-reacting mode</i>).<br/>I can’t find enough words to say because it would be too repetitive. I have read twelve (12) of his outstanding novels and this is by far, his <b>BEST</b>! I cannot recommend it highly enough. It’s too breathtaking! I cried when I finish</span>
  <span id="freeText3821538866816513868" style="display:none">“You have two choices. you can keep running and hiding and blaming the world for your problems, or you can stand up for yourself and decide to be somebody important.” —Sidney Sheldon, Nothing Lasts Forever<br /><br />Once again, I owe my life to Sidney Sheldon (<i>over-reacting mode</i>).<br />I can’t find enough words to say because it would be too repetitive. I have read twelve (12) of his outstanding novels and this is by far, his <b>BEST</b>! I cannot recommend it highly enough. It’s too breathtaking! I cried when I finished reading the novel, and the book spoke to me and said, Nothing Lasts Forever. Even the good things never last. And that I am just under the spell of Sheldon, another Book Hangover. I bet it will take days before I start reading another novel because school is at my door steps and I am still living in this book’s world.<br /><br />The novel addresses one of the roots of debates all around the world, <b>
  <i>the mercy killing</i>
</b> or Euthanasia. <b>
  <i>Euthanasia</i>
</b> is the act or practice of killing or permitting the death of hopelessly sick or injured individuals in a relatively painless way as possible. There are different perspective, opinions and ideas towards Euthanasia that is why it is not practice in some parts of the world. And in the novel, our beautiful protagonist is half-heartedly a Pro-Euthanasia.<br /><br />Moreover, the book tackles <b>
  <i>discrimination in gender and color</i>
</b> because our characters are all female doctors, one is beautiful, smart &amp; belongs to the middle-class, Dr Paige Taylor, the other is Dr Honey Taft, a very rich but self-doubted and secretive person and last but not the least, the smartest among the rest, the beautiful black woman, Dr. Kat Hunter. Don't forget that back in the early 20th century, <i>Medical Doctor</i> is a profession dominated by men and people on the highest social class. <br /><br />And lastly, the novel covertly reminds the readers (especially aspiring, practicing and full-time doctors) the value of the <b>
  <i>Hippocratic Oath</i>
</b>. It is said in the healer's Oath that they have made a promise to save lives. Pledging to the oath is an act of one who, when lawfully required to tell the truth, takes God to witness that what he says is true. It is a religious act by which the party invokes God not only to witness the truth and sincerity of his promise, but also to avenge his imposture or violated faith, or in other words to punish his false swearing if he shall be guilty of it [Legal Dictionary: Oath]. Therefore, when one takes oath he/she made a binding promise to God to do or say something lawfully and ethically. An oath is constituently related to all of the professions around the world because it obliged man to never betray humanity and to continue creating a world free from danger that leads abruptly to death.<br /><br />It is very rare to come across a book that is well-written. The characters are all winsome, especially the protagonist, one of the female doctors, Paige Turner. She's too smart, too kind and too lovable.<br />Sidney Sheldon created another one-of-a-kind novel that follows a twisty plot with his extraordinary Sheldon unpredictable ending!<br /><br />This novel is simply the best.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3821538866816513868" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1984152019" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1984152019" />
    <a title="Crime Addict Sifat" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/67289689-crime-addict-sifat"><img alt="Crime Addict Sifat" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1568459991p2/67289689.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1984152019?book_show_action=true">Apr 27, 2017</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1984152019" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer636508390615185858">Three youthful specialists their expectations, their fantasies, their sudden cravings... Dr. Paige Taylor: She swore it was willful extermination, yet when Paige acquired a million dollars from a patient, the D.A. called it kill. Dr. Kat Hunter: She pledged never to let another man excessively close again-until the point when she acknowledged the test of a lethal wager. Dr. Nectar Taft: To make it in solution, she knew she'd require something more than the brains God gave her. Dashing from the l</span>
  <span id="freeText636508390615185858" style="display:none">Three youthful specialists their expectations, their fantasies, their sudden cravings... Dr. Paige Taylor: She swore it was willful extermination, yet when Paige acquired a million dollars from a patient, the D.A. called it kill. Dr. Kat Hunter: She pledged never to let another man excessively close again-until the point when she acknowledged the test of a lethal wager. Dr. Nectar Taft: To make it in solution, she knew she'd require something more than the brains God gave her. Dashing from the life-and-demise choices of a major significant clinic to the pressure stuffed firecrackers of a murder trial, Nothing Lasts Forever exposes the aspirations and fears of healers and executioners, sweethearts and traitors. Furthermore, demonstrates at the end of the day that no peruser can outguess Sidney Sheldon, the ace of the unforeseen..<br /><br />“You know, it's not fair. Women are judged inferior until we prove ourselves, and men are judged superior until they prove what assholes they are.” <br />― Nothing Lasts Forever</span>

<div id="review_1121839318" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1121839318" />
    <a title="Janie Johnson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5116650-janie-johnson"><img alt="Janie Johnson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1486148700p2/5116650.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1121839318?book_show_action=true">Dec 02, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Janie Johnson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Janie Johnson" href="/user/show/5116650-janie-johnson">Janie Johnson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780688084912" href="/book/show/1215530.Nothing_Lasts_Forever">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5116650-janie-johnson?shelf=2014-challenge">2014-challenge</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1121839318" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3856355513960118807">Sidney Sheldon is a first time read for me and I have to ask myself why I had never picked up one of his books before now. I think that he is a brilliant writer and I am glad that I finally had the opportunity to pick up one of his books. I was totally engrossed in the story and really hated for it to end.<br/><br/>In this book we have the stories of 3 different female doctors working in the same hospital. Dr. Paige Taylor, who is on trial for the murder of a patient that she testifies was a euthanasia, D</span>
  <span id="freeText3856355513960118807" style="display:none">Sidney Sheldon is a first time read for me and I have to ask myself why I had never picked up one of his books before now. I think that he is a brilliant writer and I am glad that I finally had the opportunity to pick up one of his books. I was totally engrossed in the story and really hated for it to end.<br /><br />In this book we have the stories of 3 different female doctors working in the same hospital. Dr. Paige Taylor, who is on trial for the murder of a patient that she testifies was a euthanasia, Dr. Kat Hunter, who gets involved with a deadly bet, and Dr. Honey Taft who feels forced to becoming a doctor and does everything besides her job. Each one of these doctors are fighting their own separate demons and trying to overcome some horrific obstacles while at the same time causing some serious problems with the hospital they were all employed at.<br /><br />Most of the story has a setting inside of the Embarcadero hospital in San Francisco. The author writes the hospital with such realism that readers can visualize themselves there among the doctors, patients and their families. It seemed like with the turn of every page something new came to light for these 3 women wreaking havoc in their lives and the lives of other surrounding doctors they worked with. This story also had a lot of great back story on each of the women that allows the readers to connect to them better and also made them become far more believable and realistic.<br /><br />I loved the characters in the story. They were so well developed. So much better than I could ever explain in this review. They were less than perfect, but perfect with their flaws and shortcomings as the dealt with the everyday problems they were faced with both in the hospital setting and in their own personal lives. I felt so strongly for them, each one in a different way, and I love when an author can do that for his readers. I felt so much emotion and three women will not be easily forgotten.<br /><br />I recommend this book to anyone who loves adult medical thrillers, and mysteries. This story has so many different elements to it, love, friendship, rage, hate, jealousy, envy, honesty and trust. I think really anyone could enjoy this book because the writing is amazing. I will be sure to pick up more from Sidney Sheldon in the future.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3856355513960118807" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1818324281" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4861671029430590257">One of the few Sheldon books I didn't like. And that surprised me because I love almost everything by him. He is still one of my all time favorite writers. I just did not like this one.<br/><br/>Maybe it is because nearly all of it takes place in a hospital. For whatever reason, I felt it lacked the signature power Sheldon creates in his books. This book is about three female doctors and I did not really enjoy the story. <br/><br/>It was quite gloomy, lacking is usual "twists" and some of the stories were really up</span>
  <span id="freeText4861671029430590257" style="display:none">One of the few Sheldon books I didn't like. And that surprised me because I love almost everything by him. He is still one of my all time favorite writers. I just did not like this one.<br /><br />Maybe it is because nearly all of it takes place in a hospital. For whatever reason, I felt it lacked the signature power Sheldon creates in his books. This book is about three female doctors and I did not really enjoy the story. <br /><br />It was quite gloomy, lacking is usual "twists" and some of the stories were really upsetting. I will also say it seemed very different then most of his works.<br /><br />While not horrible, I had to push myself to chug forward on this one. Although I love Sheldon and have read almost all his books. I found this book difficult to read.<br /><br />All three of the Doctors are haunted about SOMETHING and all three of them get involved in serious issues revolving around the hospital where they work. Parts of it were Maudlin , parts were gloomy and parts were frankly just a downer.<br /><br />I hate to rate anything by this wonderful writer under a three or four. Nothing Lasts Forever, though, did not even feel like a traditional Sheldon book.<br /><br />SPOILERS:<br /><br />Also part of my distaste comes from the book morphing into a horror novel halfway through. And it morphs into a GRAPHIC horror novel. There is no suspect..we know who did it. I just..I felt like I was watching a Criminal Minds episode. Maybe some people would like that aspect but it did not do it for me.<br /><br />With all Sheldon's works, I suppose it is inevitable that there would be SOMETHING I would not like. It is also important to note that a two for a Sheldon book is equivalent to a three for 90 percent of books because Sheldon writes so incredibly even with a book I did not like.</span>

  <span id="freeText3045294544184404461" style="display:none">If I had to choose one of his books to call my utmost favorite I would have to say this one.<br /><br />Again and again he did.         <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer824031299" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer3527732259153485172"> <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1429133159ra/14535471.gif' width='500' height='380' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I've always loved a good suspense and mystery. After all, I grew up reading Sherlock Holmes rather than reading Princess stories.<br/><br/>All through out my high school year, I read all of Sidney Sheldon's books starting with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/43326.Tell_Me_Your_Dreams' title='Tell Me Your Dreams by Sidney Sheldon' rel='nofollow noopener'>Tell Me Your Dreams</a>. I was hooked after the first page. <b>No kidding.</b> Sheldon can do that to you.<br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/43325.Nothing_Lasts_Forever' title='Nothing Lasts Forever by Sidney Sheldon' rel='nofollow noopener'>Nothing Lasts Forever</a> is one of my favorite books. I still remember my struggle with this one. A classmate has a copy of this beauty and I know she doesn't read novels much alone our text</span>
  <span id="freeText3527732259153485172" style="display:none"> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1429133159ra/14535471.gif" width="500" height="380" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I've always loved a good suspense and mystery. After all, I grew up reading Sherlock Holmes rather than reading Princess stories.<br><br>All through out my high school year, I read all of Sidney Sheldon's books starting with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/43326.Tell_Me_Your_Dreams" title="Tell Me Your Dreams by Sidney Sheldon" rel="nofollow noopener">Tell Me Your Dreams</a>. I was hooked after the first page. <b>No kidding.</b> Sheldon can do that to you.<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/43325.Nothing_Lasts_Forever" title="Nothing Lasts Forever by Sidney Sheldon" rel="nofollow noopener">Nothing Lasts Forever</a> is one of my favorite books. I still remember my struggle with this one. A classmate has a copy of this beauty and I know she doesn't read novels much alone our textbooks. I don't know why she has a Sheldon book. She's more like the type of person to buy shoes than books. Anyway, I asked her if I can borrow it and guess what? The bitch <b> won't</b> lend me her copy. Her reason: <b> She just don't like sharing her things.</b> <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1416044571ra/11882374.gif" width="500" height="248" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>That crushed me. Honestly.<br><br>But the book-gods love me so much.You know what happened? We have this big individual project that takes up around 30% of our grades and because Bitchy is a part of our dance troupe, she doesn't have the time to work on that certain project.<br><br> <i> How stereotypical is that?</i><br><br>Of course, I saw my opportunity. What I did, I gave her an offer she can't refuse. <u>
  <i> I'm not talking about sex guys. Just to be clear</i>
</u><br><br><i>*Shhh*</i> I <s>manipulated</s> offered to do her project in exchange of the book. All hush hush of course. Guess what's her answer?<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<b>YES</b>  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>So I get to read the book, plus own it. She get to maintain her grades.<br><br><b>Happy ever after.</b><br><br>So back to the book.<br><br>Nothing lasts forever is a total mind-fuck book. All of Sheldon's books are mind-fucks actually. What I love about this is that, it portrays the strength of women and FYI, this book was published when women rights are not yet fully acknowledged. (Even today, some assholes are still against Women Rights)<br><br>So if you want an <b> book so expertly written that suspense, mystery and betrayal are the main dish plus a dessert of sex and ambition</b> then you better start reading this book.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="3527732259153485172" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer786698586290196717">Three female doctors begin five years in training at Embarcadero County Hospital in San Francisco. The story, set against hospital and courtroom, chronicles their lives together and their struggle against those who are determined to see that they don't succeed.<br/><br/>Dr. Paige Taylor - After she inherited a million dollars from a patient whom she 'helped to die' at their request, the District Attorney charged her with murder.<br/><br/>Dr. Kat Hunter - She vowed never to allow a man to get too close to her again.</span>
  <span id="freeText786698586290196717" style="display:none">Three female doctors begin five years in training at Embarcadero County Hospital in San Francisco. The story, set against hospital and courtroom, chronicles their lives together and their struggle against those who are determined to see that they don't succeed.<br /><br />Dr. Paige Taylor - After she inherited a million dollars from a patient whom she 'helped to die' at their request, the District Attorney charged her with murder.<br /><br />Dr. Kat Hunter - She vowed never to allow a man to get too close to her again...until she accepted the challenge of a deadly bet.<br /><br />Dr. Honey Taft - To make it in medicine, she knew that she'd need something more then the brains God gave her.<br /><br />From the life-and-death decisions faced in the operating room to the tension-packed fireworks of a murder trial, Nothing Lasts Forever by Sidney Sheldon lays bare the ambitions and fears of healers and killers, lovers and betrayers.<br /><br />I really enjoyed this book. It was a wonderful page-turner that I couldn't put down! I do so enjoy Sidney Sheldon as an author, even though I have just recently got back into reading his books after an hiatus of several years. I give this book an A+!<br /></span>

  <span id="freeText12055673119631310763" style="display:none">This was a thoroughly enjoyable book.It could easily make a plot for a soap opera. Three female doctors Paige,Kat and Honey are the main protagonists of this drama. This is definitely not a masterpiece but it's readable and definitely keeps the reader interested. Is Paige Taylor innocent or guilty?From the beginning of the book the young doctor is accused of murdering a patient and inheriting 1.000.000 dollars and then the writer goes back in time and unravels this interesting drama. Three and a half stars from me.</span>

<div id="review_1047880889" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1047880889" />
    <a title="Kris" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/34714367-kris"><img alt="Kris" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1047880889?book_show_action=true">Sep 06, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kris" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kris" href="/user/show/34714367-kris">Kris</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1047880889" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2726904751865467050">This book is weird.<br/><br/>Here are some examples of things that are said and done in this book:<br/><br/>**"In the uncomfortable backseat of Merton's car, Honey had sex for the first time....she did not particularly enjoy it, but that was not important. The important thing was that Merton enjoyed it.....So this is how I please a man, Honey thought."<br/><br/>Honey makes me want to bang my head against a wall. There can't possibly be girls like her in the world, right? I need there to not be girls like that in the world. O</span>
  <span id="freeText2726904751865467050" style="display:none">This book is weird.<br /><br />Here are some examples of things that are said and done in this book:<br /><br />**"In the uncomfortable backseat of Merton's car, Honey had sex for the first time....she did not particularly enjoy it, but that was not important. The important thing was that Merton enjoyed it.....So this is how I please a man, Honey thought."<br /><br />Honey makes me want to bang my head against a wall. There can't possibly be girls like her in the world, right? I need there to not be girls like that in the world. Or at the very least this needs to have been a 90s thing.<br /><br />**At one point there is a line about a doctor, nicknamed 007, who the book says "[takes] out organs that were healthy." In what world would NO ONE in a hospital do anything about this?! But wait! It gets worse! Another resident actually says to Paige, when she brings this up, "Calm down. I'll take you out and buy you lunch."<br /><br />I mean, REALLY?!<br /><br />**The girls get the bright idea to throw a party to cheer themselves up. Except they throw said party AT THE HOSPITAL. And then when everyone gets paged and has to go back to saving lives, (y'know, that thing they do IN A HOSPITAL) one of them actually says, "I can't believe what's happening."<br /><br />CAN'T YOU?<br /><br />**Kat introduces herself as follows:<br /><br />"I'm Kate Hunter. They call me Kat."<br /><br />Kate and Kat are BOTH short forms of Katherine. If you prefer Kat, why are you introducing yourself as Kate?!<br /><br />**There is a typo on the first page. Seriously.<br /><br />**Honey says that she has bad luck with men, and Kat says that maybe she'll have better luck at the hospital. Because when you're a woman just starting your career in a male dominated field, you would absolutely think this way.<br /><br />And there's more:<br /><br />Paige finds out that she's going to be working with a world-renowned doctor, whom she has never met, nor even seen a picture of, and before she even meets him she HAS A SEX DREAM ABOUT HIM.<br /><br />REALLY?! It was at this point I started to think this book had to be a joke. Like maybe somebody swapped out the real copy for this ridiculousness. Because this book has gotten good reviews and I honestly don't understand why.<br /><br />**There are SO MANY things wrong with the chapter where Jason and Paige meet. First of all, he calls the hospital and asks for her home number, and a secretary JUST GIVES IT TO HIM, without even asking WHY he wants it. Oh, and when he shows up for their first date, she's asleep in the on call room. A nurse tells him where she is, instead of calling her, and then he goes in and just WATCHES HER SLEEP. It's creepy. And apparently at this point he already thinks he's going to marry her.<br /><br />For their second date, he takes her to MEET HIS PARENTS. Their SECOND date! Guys, this is so. creepy.<br /><br />Oh, and on said date, she falls asleep at the dinner table. Like, head falls straight down on the table. In front of his parents. While there is food on the table.<br /><br />I mean, COME ON.<br /><br />**At one point there's a patient who it turns out has cholera, and the administrator decides to cover it up because it would hurt the hospital, and we're supposed to believe that EVERYONE is totally fine to go along with this.<br /><br />REALLY?!<br /><br />**The part where Paige euthanizes the patient she winds up on trial for murdering is weird. She takes all of three seconds to agree to do it. And then she does it right away. No second guessing. No discussing it with her colleagues or Kat and Honey. And it says that the patient only had a few days to live. I'm pro-DAS, but even I thought that if he's only got a few days left, why do it? It would obviously lead to some problems for her, so why bring all of that trouble down on herself over the difference of a few days?<br /><br />**Paige doesn't know that her boyfriend and future husband has married someone else until he shows up on her doorstep with his new wife.<br /><br />SERIOUSLY?!<br /><br />So yeah. This book is weird. A lot of the lines and situations just seem so ridiculous, like they'd never happen.<br /><br />The author wrote for television before he started writing novels, and it shows. The book reads like a script. It's mostly just dialogue and the scenes move very quickly. It jumps between scenes and characters in a really odd way. Kind of like you'd see on TV. The lack of descriptive passages isn't entirely a negative, because I generally find descriptive passages to be boring, and making it dialogue-heavy makes the book a quick read, but at the very least I would expect a portion of the book to be dedicated to what was going on in a character's head in between the dialogue.<br /><br />Mostly I was just disappointed that the author couldn't shift from the one medium to the other. In fact, the epilogue reads EXACTLY like the end to a movie based on a true story, where they tell you what happened to each of the real-life people after the movie ends.<br /><br />The thing that's a real shame is it actually starts to get good toward the end. It stays on one narrative - none of that weird jumping between brief scenes that have nothing to do with each other - and the story actually becomes interesting. But then the book is over, so....<br /><br />Basically, this guy should have stuck to TV.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2726904751865467050" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer55114337" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7244902183475982651">I've never read any Sidney Sheldon before, but he does a wonderful job of drawing the plot along. Most mysteries are pretty straight forward -- sure there are plot twists, and the mystery may be hard to guess, but the way the story itself is written is pretty straight forward. In this book the author actually switches it up a bit, starting the story with a scene from the court case which leaves you with one possible interpretation of the facts, and you spend the rest of the novel learning whethe</span>
  <span id="freeText7244902183475982651" style="display:none">I've never read any Sidney Sheldon before, but he does a wonderful job of drawing the plot along. Most mysteries are pretty straight forward -- sure there are plot twists, and the mystery may be hard to guess, but the way the story itself is written is pretty straight forward. In this book the author actually switches it up a bit, starting the story with a scene from the court case which leaves you with one possible interpretation of the facts, and you spend the rest of the novel learning whether or not it's the correct interpretation. It's a small literary device, but it made a <i>huge</i> difference to the overall quality of the book.<br /><br />Add to that a good plot and a couple of very well written dialogue sections, and you have a real winner.<br /><br />And also, I'm pretty sure the writers for Grey's Anatomy have read this book, because some of their plots sound like they could have been lifted (or at the very least inspired) from this book...</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_942565865" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/942565865" />
    <a title="Ashwani Pandey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22199944-ashwani-pandey"><img alt="Ashwani Pandey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1466957915p2/22199944.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/942565865?book_show_action=true">May 19, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashwani Pandey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashwani Pandey" href="/user/show/22199944-ashwani-pandey">Ashwani Pandey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer942565865" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3423370869881562622">Well, all thanks to this novel for it added all the necessary ingredients to make my trip back home an awesome one and yep thanks to my dear friend too who suggested it to me. It was my first novel of Sidney Sheldon and ye i loved the story telling and i am already on my way for his second novel "If Tomorrow Comes" and i am sure i would love this one too.<br/><br/>The story has many things in it, ranging from<b> male dominance </b> to how bad someone's greed can be, to<b> how hard a doctor's life is</b>. Starting with </span>
  <span id="freeText3423370869881562622" style="display:none">Well, all thanks to this novel for it added all the necessary ingredients to make my trip back home an awesome one and yep thanks to my dear friend too who suggested it to me. It was my first novel of Sidney Sheldon and ye i loved the story telling and i am already on my way for his second novel "If Tomorrow Comes" and i am sure i would love this one too.<br /><br />The story has many things in it, ranging from<b> male dominance </b> to how bad someone's greed can be, to<b> how hard a doctor's life is</b>. Starting with that of male dominance, i can say that it's not of that level as described in the book knowing the fact that the book was published in 1994. Ofcourse things would have been like that only in those days. But you just can't ignore it for the present society because that stupid dominance still does exist <b>(and more than that it's the sexist comments people do make or harass women in some way or the other)</b> and we all can feel it, the only thing being that the level has gone down with time, thanks to the determined efforts of the women as well as the awareness that is spreading in the society.<br /><br />Then i was also lost in my thoughts<b> while reading the daily schedule of a doctor as was described.</b> I can for sure take some lessons from that but at the same time, such a scenario still does exist in government hospitals and that's very dangerous from two points. Firstly most of the good doctors want a good payment, so why would they work for govt. hospitals where the load is too much, when instead they can work for private hospitals or set up their own private practice and live a luxurious life thereafter. And then you are left with doctors like Arthur Kane who can operate on your good kidney leaving you on dialysis forever.<br />Secondly, when a doctor works for such long hours, he/she is surely to feel frustrated and this is not good for it leaves no time for themselves or their families and this might lead to some disastrous results as was the case with Tom Chang.<br /><br />It was also inspiring to read of the childhood of Paige and especially of her father. It's natural to me to feel inspired when i read of someone like him. Even though he was a fictional character, people like him do exist and they do motivate us to do some good for the society. Then the childhood of Honey do show us the pressure of performing well in a brainy family. But it does give an insight to the case of honey traps which is surely not a good thing at all, whatever case it may be. This led to the wrong diagnosis of her patients, however we cannot blame Honey for it. A large share goes to her parents who never respected her feelings and this surely gives us the lesson<b> that every child is born different </b>and you can never pressurise them for something they don't want to become, and their feelings need to be respected and they should not be mocked for their ideas for they would then never share anything with you.<br /><br />Then there are people like Kat who never lived their childhood, rather it was some kind of horror for them.The words of her aunt were truly inspiring.<b> "You can keep running and hiding and blaming the world for your problems ,or you can stand up for yourself and decide to be somebody important by knowing that you're important. First you get an image in your mind of who you want to be, child, and what you want to be. And then you go to work, becoming that person."</b><br /><br />Not to forget Barker. People like him do exist whom we hate so much that we always wish something bad for them or atleast wish to get rid of them, the reason being their cold and arrogant nature towards us. But these are the people who want something good for us and are always there to extend their helping hand.<br />There were many other characters like that of Ken, who could even kill someone for his greed or Alfred, whose work didn't surprise me that much for that can happen with anyone given the circumstances.<br /><br />Then,<b> what about the title of the novel NOTHING LASTS FOREVER...</b> I was thinking of it and the sense that it made to me was that all the three of female doctors had to go through different phases of joy and sorrow in their lives and may be that's what life is all about. Nothing is permanent out there. And if extended further, the same can be said for the relationships that we do share with different people throughout our life.<br /><br />And finally the person of the novel. It's difficult one to choose,but I am more inclined towards Paige Taylor than anyone else for all her characteristics that Sheldon has shown to us. Overall a marvelous storytelling and looking forward to read more novels of him!</span>
  <a data-text-id="3423370869881562622" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText6118634302259008311" style="display:none">started 5/19/09<br /><br />Oh, Lord, I am DONE with this! I don't think I can give it any stars....can't say I liked but can't say I didn't like it either, because it sure was entertaining! If I hadn't had to work, this book would have been finished within 24 hours.<br /><br />Like I told Bob, I should have left Sheldon in my pre-adolescent childhood, because I never realized just how overly dramatic and "soap opera-ly" he is. The dialogue is horrible and superficial. There is no depth to the story at all. We won't even get into how horrible the medical facts are. In the beginning of the novel there is a gratitude statement to all of the doctors, nurses, and techs who "provided their expertise" to him. He either didn't listen close enough, or maybe things really were different in the early 90s, who knows?<br /><br />If there is one thing this novel has taught me, it's to never read Sheldon again. And I think he's dead now, so that shouldn't be a problem.<br /><br />Fine since I can't seem to talk myself out of leaving the stars blank, I'm giving it 2.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4299965510504043471">"Women are judged inferior until we prove ourselves, and men are judged superior until they prove what assholes they are." - Sidney Sheldon, Nothing Lasts Forever.<br/><br/>Is there anything that lasts forever?<br/>If this question is answerable, then Sidney Sheldon has put into words quite well in the perception of "life is unpredictable".<br/>Life transforms all the time. <br/>If you gain something, then you lose something.<br/>The unpredictability makes life challenging and often test our character.<br/>People who stuck in a d</span>
  <span id="freeText4299965510504043471" style="display:none">"Women are judged inferior until we prove ourselves, and men are judged superior until they prove what assholes they are." - Sidney Sheldon, Nothing Lasts Forever.<br /><br />Is there anything that lasts forever?<br />If this question is answerable, then Sidney Sheldon has put into words quite well in the perception of "life is unpredictable".<br />Life transforms all the time. <br />If you gain something, then you lose something.<br />The unpredictability makes life challenging and often test our character.<br />People who stuck in a deep shit have only hope of getting out of it due to this unpredictability.<br />You will never know what life has kept for you in its store.<br /><br />The book is well written and quick paced. The drama behind the story is casual and digestible.<br />The story of three women doctors who struggle in the 'men's club' where their capabilities are underestimated.<br />These women face very different challenges and obstacles but their lives beautifully intertwined.<br />Each character capture readers by their strength, heartaches and abilities which inspire them to believe in the equality of women and men.<br /><br />All around it's an exceptional thriller for Sheldon's fans.</span>

    <a title="Aparna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27204537-aparna"><img alt="Aparna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1562624263p2/27204537.jpg" /></a>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3634896090?book_show_action=true">Nov 09, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aparna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aparna" href="/user/show/27204537-aparna">Aparna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/10395883-nothing-lasts-forever">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27204537-aparna?shelf=thriller-mystery">thriller-mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3634896090" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11034441480385757619">An interesting mystery which follows the lives of three female doctors throughout their surgical residency. This was fast-paced yet didn’t miss our character development and details. <br/><br/>However it was very cliché and some of the characters’ actions were not entirely believable. <br/><br/>Still, the author doesn’t let the reader’s interest drop. A fun, quick read. </span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_2722983547" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2722983547" />
    <a title="Santhu Ghimire" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38203512-santhu-ghimire"><img alt="Santhu Ghimire" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1531473764p2/38203512.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2722983547?book_show_action=true">Feb 22, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Santhu Ghimire" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Santhu Ghimire" href="/user/show/38203512-santhu-ghimire">Santhu Ghimire</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780006476580" href="/book/show/900011.Nothing_Lasts_Forever">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38203512-santhu-ghimire?shelf=s-n-s-collection">s-n-s-collection</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2722983547" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13155662134248746447">Only one thing. <br/> You can't shock asystole. Period. That big flat line cannot be made beating again by defibrillating. You cannot bring back a patient in asystole by shocking. You need manual compress and epinephrine. <br/> I didn't expect this from Sidney Sheldon at least. He did researches on other medical things but missed this basic thing.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('oV7epNNblbQ/ZzJ+WMGyE00w2AIwldGPndOEdK0NxYuM8I7Trw5LkdiliNlv0t3osQfKERxrrobeHrAmMQe2Yw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ykw2NUWQi2OrD4v7k5tyDSHw1jDKWu5uJKMloHpsiAfn4mZCOcVVRkzNMVykiB323cfEI+akkWdnbhHy5mb77w==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/9068.Sidney_Sheldon"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1209169297p3/9068.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer2950947552835090523">Sidney Sheldon (1917-2007) was an American writer who won awards in three careers—a Broadway playwright, a Hollywood TV and movie screenwriter, and a best-selling novelist.<br/><br/>His TV works spanned a twenty-year period during which he created <i>I Dream of Jeannie</i> (1965-70), <i>Hart to Hart</i> (1979-84), and <i>The Patty Duke Show</i> (1963-66), but it was not until after he turned 50 and began writing best-selling no</span>
  <span id="freeText2950947552835090523" style="display:none">Sidney Sheldon (1917-2007) was an American writer who won awards in three careers—a Broadway playwright, a Hollywood TV and movie screenwriter, and a best-selling novelist.<br /><br />His TV works spanned a twenty-year period during which he created <i>I Dream of Jeannie</i> (1965-70), <i>Hart to Hart</i> (1979-84), and <i>The Patty Duke Show</i> (1963-66), but it was not until after he turned 50 and began writing best-selling novels such as <i>Master of the Game</i> (1982), <i>The Other Side of Midnight</i> (1973) and <i>Rage of Angels</i> (1980) that he became most famous.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2950947552835090523" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
